      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FWM-WSB_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FWM-WSB-84">
        [81]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Realf" title="Richard Realf">
       Richard Realf
      </a>
      , while poet and writer
      <a href="/wiki/Hilaire_Belloc" title="Hilaire Belloc">
       Hilaire Belloc
      </a>
      spent most of his life in Sussex.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Percy_Bysshe_Shelley_by_Alfred_Clint.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2948" data-file-width="2400" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Percy_Bysshe_Shelley_by_Alfred_Clint.jpg/150px-Percy_Bysshe_Shelley_by_Alfred_Clint.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Percy_Bysshe_Shelley_by_Alfred_Clint.jpg/225px-Percy_Bysshe_Shelley_by_Alfred_Clint.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Percy_Bysshe_Shelley_by_Alfred_Clint.jpg/300px-Percy_Bysshe_Shelley_by_Alfred_Clint.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Percy_Bysshe_Shelley_by_Alfred_Clint.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Percy Bysshe Shelley is one of Sussex's best-known poets
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Sheila_Kaye-Smith" title="Sheila Kaye-Smith">
       Sheila Kaye-Smith
      </a>
      is known for her many novels in the
      <a href="/wiki/British_regional_literature" title="British regional literature">
       British regional literature
      </a>
      genre, which are set in the borderlands of Sussex and
      <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">
       Kent
      </a>
      . Other writers from Sussex include
      <a href="/wiki/Maureen_Duffy" title="Maureen Duffy">
       Maureen Duffy
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hammond_Innes" title="Hammond Innes">
       Hammond Innes
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In addition there are writers, who while they were not born in Sussex had a strong connection. This includes
      <a href="/wiki/William_Blake" title="William Blake">
       William Blake
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfred_Tennyson" title="Alfred Tennyson">
       Alfred Tennyson
      </a>
      . Sussex has been home to four winners of the
      <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">
       Nobel Prize in Literature
      </a>
      :
      <a href="/wiki/Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling">
       Rudyard Kipling
      </a>
      spent much of his life in Sussex, living in Rottingdean and later at Burwash.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        [82]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Irishman
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/W.B._Yeats" title="W.B. Yeats">
       W.B. Yeats
      </a>
      spent three winters living with American poet
      <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Pound" title="Ezra Pound">
       Ezra Pound
      </a>
      at Colemans Hatch in the Ashdown Forest
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OddCouple_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-OddCouple-86">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and towards the end of his life spent much time at Steyning and Withyham;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CritComp_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CritComp-87">
        [84]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/John_Galsworthy" title="John Galsworthy">
       John Galsworthy
      </a>
      spent much of his life in Bury in the Sussex Downs;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SD-Oth_88-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SD-Oth-88">
        [85]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Harold_Pinter" title="Harold Pinter">
       Harold Pinter
      </a>
      lived in Worthing in the 1960s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ParRev_89-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ParRev-89">
        [86]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      H.G. Wells was brought up at
      <a href="/wiki/Uppark" title="Uppark">
       Uppark
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/South_Harting" title="South Harting">
       South Harting
      </a>
      , near
      <a href="/wiki/Petersfield" title="Petersfield">
       Petersfield
      </a>
      , where his mother was housekeeper. He also went to school and taught in
      <a href="/wiki/Midhurst" title="Midhurst">
       Midhurst
      </a>
      . While the novelist
      <a href="/wiki/John_Cowper_Powys" title="John Cowper Powys">
       John Cowper Powys
      </a>
      is particularly associated with
      <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">
       Dorset
      </a>
      and Wales, he lived in Sussex from the mid-1890s until 1910.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        [87]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modernist" title="Modernist">
       modernist
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Woolf" title="Virginia Woolf">
       Virginia Woolf
      </a>
      (1882-1941) and her husband
      <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Woolf" title="Leonard Woolf">
       Leonard
      </a>
      , had a country retreat at
      <a href="/wiki/Monk%27s_House" title="Monk's House">
       Monk's House
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Rodmell" title="Rodmell">
       Rodmell
      </a>
      near in
      <a href="/wiki/Lewes" title="Lewes">
       Lewes
      </a>
      from 1919. They received there many important visitors connected to the
      <a href="/wiki/Bloomsbury_Group" title="Bloomsbury Group">
       Bloomsbury Group
      </a>
      , including
      <a href="/wiki/T._S._Eliot" title="T. S. Eliot">
       T. S. Eliot
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/E._M._Forster" title="E. M. Forster">
       E. M. Forster
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Roger_Fry" title="Roger Fry">
       Roger Fry
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lytton_Strachey" title="Lytton Strachey">
       Lytton Strachey
      </a>
      . Scottish writer
      <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Arthur Conan Doyle">
       Arthur Conan Doyle
      </a>
      (1859-1930) spent the last thirty years of his life in
      <a href="/wiki/Crowborough" title="Crowborough">
       Crowborough
      </a>
      . In 1897
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_James" title="Henry James">
       Henry James
      </a>
      (1843-1916) leased
      <a href="/wiki/Lamb_House" title="Lamb House">
       Lamb House
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Rye" title="Rye">
       Rye
      </a>
      , and purchasing it two years later, spent most of his last 18 years there, where he wrote several major works. Lamb House was subsequently home to both
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_Frederic_Benson" title="Edward Frederic Benson">
       E.F. Benson
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Rumer_Godden" title="Rumer Godden">
       Rumer Godden
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AA_Milne" title="AA Milne">
       AA Milne
      </a>
      lived in Ashdown Forest for much of his life and set his
      <a href="/wiki/Winnie-the-Pooh" title="Winnie-the-Pooh">
       Winnie-the-Pooh
      </a>
      stories in the forest.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
       Music
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sussex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Music">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Sussex" title="Music of Sussex">
       Music of Sussex
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Sussex's rich musical heritage encompasses folk, classical and popular genres amongst others. Composed by William Ward-Higgs,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sussex_by_the_Sea" title="Sussex by the Sea">
        Sussex by the Sea
       </a>
      </i>
      is the county's unofficial
      <a href="/wiki/Anthem" title="Anthem">
       anthem
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxMusic_91-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxMusic-91">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Passed on through
      <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">
       oral tradition
      </a>
      , many of Sussex's traditional songs may not have changed significantly for centuries, with their origins perhaps dating as far back as the time of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Saxons" title="South Saxons">
       South Saxons
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxPeople_77-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxPeople-77">
        [74]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Hudson" title="William Henry Hudson">
       William Henry Hudson
      </a>
      compared the singing of the Sussexians with that of the
      <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">
       Basques
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Tehuelche_people" title="Tehuelche people">
       Tehuelche people
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">
       Patagonia
      </a>
      , both peoples with ancient cultures.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NIDnland_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NIDnland-92">
        [89]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The songs sung by the
      <a href="/wiki/Copper_Family" title="Copper Family">
       Copper Family
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_Burstow" title="Henry Burstow">
       Henry Burstow
      </a>
      , Samuel Willett, Peter and Harriett Verrall, David Penfold and others were collected by John Broadwood and his niece
      <a href="/wiki/Lucy_Broadwood" title="Lucy Broadwood">
       Lucy Broadwood
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kate_Lee" title="Kate Lee">
       Kate Lee
      </a>
      and composers
      <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Vaughan_Williams" title="Ralph Vaughan Williams">
       Ralph Vaughan Williams
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/George_Butterworth" title="George Butterworth">
       George Butterworth
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxMusic_91-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxMusic-91">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        [90]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sussex also played a major part in the folk music revival of the 1960s and 1970s with various singers including George 'Pop' Maynard,
      <a href="/wiki/Scan_Tester" title="Scan Tester">
       Scan Tester
      </a>
      , Tony Wales and the sisters
      <a href="/wiki/Dolly_Collins" title="Dolly Collins">
       Dolly
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Collins" title="Shirley Collins">
       Shirley Collins
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxMusic_91-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxMusic-91">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Cure_Live_in_Singapore_2-_1st_August_2007.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Cure_Live_in_Singapore_2-_1st_August_2007.jpg/150px-The_Cure_Live_in_Singapore_2-_1st_August_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Cure_Live_in_Singapore_2-_1st_August_2007.jpg/225px-The_Cure_Live_in_Singapore_2-_1st_August_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/The_Cure_Live_in_Singapore_2-_1st_August_2007.jpg/300px-The_Cure_Live_in_Singapore_2-_1st_August_2007.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Cure_Live_in_Singapore_2-_1st_August_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Cure performing live in Singapore
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Sussex has also been home to many composers of classical music including
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Weelkes" title="Thomas Weelkes">
       Thomas Weelkes
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Ireland_(composer)" title="John Ireland (composer)">
       John Ireland
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edward_Elgar" title="Edward Elgar">
       Edward Elgar
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Frank_Bridge" title="Frank Bridge">
       Frank Bridge
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Hubert_Parry" title="Sir Hubert Parry">
       Sir Hubert Parry
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Vaughan_Williams" title="Ralph Vaughan Williams">
       Ralph Vaughan Williams
      </a>
      , who played a major part in recording Sussex's traditional music.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxMusic_91-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxMusic-91">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
      While
      <a href="/wiki/Glyndebourne" title="Glyndebourne">
       Glyndebourne
      </a>
      is one of the world's best known opera houses, the county is home to professional orchestras the Brighton Philharmonic Orchestra
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPO_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BPO-94">
        [91]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Worthing_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Worthing Symphony Orchestra">
       Worthing Symphony Orchestra
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSO_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WSO-95">
        [92]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">
       popular music
      </a>
      , Sussex has produced artists including
      <a href="/wiki/Leo_Sayer" title="Leo Sayer">
       Leo Sayer
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Cure" title="The Cure">
       The Cure
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Levellers_(band)" title="Levellers (band)">
       The Levellers
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Brett_Anderson" title="Brett Anderson">
       Brett Anderson
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Keane_(band)" title="Keane (band)">
       Keane
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Kooks" title="The Kooks">
       The Kooks
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Feeling" title="The Feeling">
       The Feeling
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rizzle_Kicks" title="Rizzle Kicks">
       Rizzle Kicks
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Conor_Maynard" title="Conor Maynard">
       Conor Maynard
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tom_Odell" title="Tom Odell">
       Tom Odell
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Royal_Blood_(band)" title="Royal Blood (band)">
       Royal Blood
      </a>
      . In the 1970s, Sussex was home to
      <a href="/wiki/Phun_City" title="Phun City">
       Phun City
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKRF-PhunCity_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UKRF-PhunCity-96">
        [93]
       </a>
      </sup>
      the UK's first large-scale free music festival and hosted the
      <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_1974" title="Eurovision Song Contest 1974">
       1974 Eurovision Song Contest
      </a>
      which propelled
      <a href="/wiki/ABBA" title="ABBA">
       ABBA
      </a>
      to worldwide fame. Major festivals include
      <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Escape_Festival" title="The Great Escape Festival">
       The Great Escape Festival
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardTGE_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GuardTGE-97">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Glyndebourne_Festival_Opera" title="Glyndebourne Festival Opera">
       Glyndebourne Festival Opera
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
       Religion
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sussex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Religion">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Sussex is connected with several saints, including
      <a href="/wiki/Leofwynn" title="Leofwynn">
       St Lewina
      </a>
      ;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Wilfrid" title="St Wilfrid">
       St Wilfrid
      </a>
      , sometimes known as the 'Apostle of Sussex';
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuthman_of_Steyning" title="Cuthman of Steyning">
       St Cuthman of Steyning
      </a>
      ;
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Richard_of_Chichester" title="St Richard of Chichester">
       St Richard of Chichester
      </a>
      , Sussex's patron saint;
      <a href="/wiki/Philip_Howard,_20th_Earl_of_Arundel" title="Philip Howard, 20th Earl of Arundel">
       St Philip Howard, Earl of Arundel
      </a>
      ; and
      <a href="/wiki/James_Hannington" title="James Hannington">
       James Hannington
      </a>
      . In folklore,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayfield,_East_Sussex" title="Mayfield, East Sussex">
       Mayfield
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Dyke,_Sussex" title="Devil's Dyke, Sussex">
       Devil's Dyke
      </a>
      are linked with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Dunstan" title="St Dunstan">
       St Dunstan
      </a>
      while
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Tarring" title="West Tarring">
       West Tarring
      </a>
      has links with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Thomas_a_Becket" title="St Thomas a Becket">
       St Thomas a Becket
      </a>
      . The historic county has been a single diocese after St Wilfrid converted the kingdom of Sussex in the seventh century. The seat of the Sussex bishopric was originally located at
      <a href="/wiki/Selsey_Abbey" title="Selsey Abbey">
       Selsey Abbey
      </a>
      before the Normans moved it to
      <a href="/wiki/Chichester_Cathedral" title="Chichester Cathedral">
       Chichester Cathedral
      </a>
      in 1075. Since 1965
      <a href="/wiki/Arundel_Cathedral" title="Arundel Cathedral">
       Arundel Cathedral
      </a>
      has been the seat of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
       Roman Catholic
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Arundel_and_Brighton" title="Bishop of Arundel and Brighton">
       Bishops of Arundel and Brighton
      </a>
      , which covers Sussex and Surrey.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arundel_Cathedral.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arundel_Cathedral.JPG/220px-Arundel_Cathedral.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arundel_Cathedral.JPG/330px-Arundel_Cathedral.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Arundel_Cathedral.JPG/440px-Arundel_Cathedral.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arundel_Cathedral.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Roman Catholic cathedral at
        <a href="/wiki/Arundel_Cathedral" title="Arundel Cathedral">
         Arundel
        </a>
        . Arundel has been a stronghold of the Catholic faith since the Reformation
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Historically, the west of the county has had a tendency towards Catholicism while the east of the county has had a tendency towards non-conformism.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        [95]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The county has been home to several pilgrimage sites, including the shrine (at Chichester Cathedral) to St Richard of Chichester which was destroyed during the Reformation, and the more recent Catholic shrine at
      <a href="/wiki/West_Grinstead" title="West Grinstead">
       West Grinstead
      </a>
      . During the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marian_persecutions" title="Marian persecutions">
       Marian persecutions
      </a>
      , several Sussex men were martyred for their Protestant faith, including 17 men at Lewes. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Society_of_Dependents" title="Society of Dependents">
       Society of Dependents
      </a>
      (nicknamed the Cokelers) were a non-conformist sect formed in Loxwood. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quaker" title="Quaker">
       Quaker
      </a>
      and founding father of
      <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">
       Pennsylvania
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">
       William Penn
      </a>
      worshipped near
      <a href="/wiki/Thakeham" title="Thakeham">
       Thakeham
      </a>
      ;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        [96]
       </a>
      </sup>
      his UK home from 1677 to 1702 was at nearby Warminghurst.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        [97]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The UK's only
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carthusian" title="Carthusian">
       Carthusian
      </a>
      monastery is situated at
      <a href="/wiki/St._Hugh%27s_Charterhouse,_Parkminster" title="St. Hugh's Charterhouse, Parkminster">
       St. Hugh's Charterhouse, Parkminster
      </a>
      near Cowfold. The UK headquarters of the
      <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scientology" title="Church of Scientology">
       Church of Scientology
      </a>
      is situated at
      <a href="/wiki/Saint_Hill_Manor" title="Saint Hill Manor">
       Saint Hill Manor
      </a>
      , near East Grinstead.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Science">
       Science
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sussex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Science">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Pell%27s_equation" title="Pell's equation">
       Pell's equation
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Pell_number" title="Pell number">
       Pell number
      </a>
      are both named after 17th century mathematician
      <a href="/wiki/John_Pell" title="John Pell">
       John Pell
      </a>
      . Pell is sometimes credited with inventing the division sign, which has also been attributed to Swiss mathematician
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johann_Heinrich_Rahn" title="Johann Heinrich Rahn">
       Johann Heinrich Rahn
      </a>
      , one of his students. In the 19th century, geologist and palaeontologist
      <a href="/wiki/Gideon_Mantell" title="Gideon Mantell">
       Gideon Mantell
      </a>
      began the scientific study of dinosaurs. In 1822 he was responsible for the discovery and eventual identification of the first fossil teeth, and later much of the skeleton of
      <a href="/wiki/Iguanodon" title="Iguanodon">
       Iguanodon
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Braxton_Hicks_contractions" title="Braxton Hicks contractions">
       Braxton Hicks contractions
      </a>
      are named after
      <a href="/wiki/John_Braxton_Hicks" title="John Braxton Hicks">
       John Braxton Hicks
      </a>
      , the Sussex doctor who in 1872 first described the uterine contractions not resulting in childbirth.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Maynard_Keynes.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="250" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/John_Maynard_Keynes.jpg/150px-John_Maynard_Keynes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/John_Maynard_Keynes.jpg/225px-John_Maynard_Keynes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/66/John_Maynard_Keynes.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Maynard_Keynes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        JM Keynes lived at Tilton near
        <a href="/wiki/Firle" title="Firle">
         Firle
        </a>
        from 1925 to 1946
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the 20th century,
      <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Soddy" title="Frederick Soddy">
       Frederick Soddy
      </a>
      won the
      <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">
       Nobel Prize in Chemistry
      </a>
      for his work on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radioactive" title="Radioactive">
       radioactive
      </a>
      substances, and his investigations into the origin and nature of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isotopes" title="Isotopes">
       isotopes
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel1921_101-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nobel1921-101">
        [98]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Gowland_Hopkins" title="Frederick Gowland Hopkins">
       Frederick Gowland Hopkins
      </a>
      shared the
      <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">
       Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine
      </a>
      in 1929 with
      <a href="/wiki/Christiaan_Eijkman" title="Christiaan Eijkman">
       Christiaan Eijkman
      </a>
      , for discovering the growth-stimulating
      <a href="/wiki/Vitamin" title="Vitamin">
       vitamins
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel1929_102-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nobel1929-102">
        [99]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Martin_Ryle" title="Martin Ryle">
       Martin Ryle
      </a>
      shared the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Physics" title="Nobel Prize for Physics">
       Nobel Prize for Physics
      </a>
      in 1974
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel_103-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nobel-103">
        [100]
       </a>
      </sup>
      with Cornishman
      <a href="/wiki/Antony_Hewish" title="Antony Hewish">
       Antony Hewish
      </a>
      , the first Nobel prize awarded in recognition of astronomical research. While working at the University of Sussex,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harold_Kroto" title="Harold Kroto">
       Harold Kroto
      </a>
      won the 1996
      <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">
       Nobel Prize in Chemistry
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Smalley" title="Richard Smalley">
       Richard Smalley
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Curl" title="Robert Curl">
       Robert Curl
      </a>
      from
      <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">
       Rice University
      </a>
      in the USA for the discovery of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fullerenes" title="Fullerenes">
       fullerenes
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel1996_104-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Nobel1996-104">
        [101]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/David_Mumford" title="David Mumford">
       David Mumford
      </a>
      is a mathematician known for distinguished work in algebraic geometry and then for research into vision and pattern theory. He won the
      <a href="/wiki/International_Mathematical_Union" title="International Mathematical Union">
       International Mathematical Union
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">
       Fields Medal
      </a>
      in 1974 and in 2010 was awarded the United States
      <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">
       National Medal of Science
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">
       social sciences
      </a>
      , Sussex was home to
      <a href="/wiki/Economist" title="Economist">
       economist
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/John_Maynard_Keynes" title="John Maynard Keynes">
       John Maynard Keynes
      </a>
      from 1925 to 1946. The founding father of
      <a href="/wiki/Keynesian_economics" title="Keynesian economics">
       Keynesian economics
      </a>
      , he is widely considered to be one of the founders of modern macroeconomics and the most influential economist of the 20th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        [103]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        [104]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        [105]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/David_Pilbeam" title="David Pilbeam">
       David Pilbeam
      </a>
      won the 1986
      <a href="/wiki/International_Prize_(Fyssen_Foundation)" title="International Prize (Fyssen Foundation)">
       International Prize
      </a>
      from the
      <a href="/wiki/Fyssen_Foundation" title="Fyssen Foundation">
       Fyssen Foundation
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fond_Fyss_109-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Fond_Fyss-109">
        [106]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the early 20th century, Sussex was at the centre of one of what has been described as 'British archaeology's greatest hoax'.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardPiltdn_110-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GuardPiltdn-110">
        [107]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Bone fragments said to have been collected in 1912 were presented as the fossilised remains of a previously unknown early human, referred to as
      <a href="/wiki/Piltdown_Man" title="Piltdown Man">
       Piltdown Man
      </a>
      . In 1953 the bone fragments were exposed as a forgery, consisting of the lower jawbone of an
      <a href="/wiki/Orangutan" title="Orangutan">
       orangutan
      </a>
      deliberately combined with the skull of a fully developed modern human. From 1967 to 1979, Sussex was home to the
      <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton_Telescope" title="Isaac Newton Telescope">
       Isaac Newton Telescope
      </a>
      at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Greenwich_Observatory" title="Royal Greenwich Observatory">
       Royal Greenwich Observatory
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Herstmonceux_Castle" title="Herstmonceux Castle">
       Herstmonceux Castle
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">
       Sport
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sussex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sport">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Sussex" title="Sport in Sussex">
       Sport in Sussex
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Sussex has a centuries-long tradition of sport. Sussex has played a key role in the early development of both
      <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">
       cricket
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Stoolball" title="Stoolball">
       stoolball
      </a>
      . Cricket is recognised as having been formed in the
      <a href="/wiki/Weald" title="Weald">
       Weald
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sussex_CCC" title="Sussex CCC">
       Sussex CCC
      </a>
      is England's oldest county cricket club.
      <a href="/wiki/Slindon_Cricket_Club" title="Slindon Cricket Club">
       Slindon Cricket Club
      </a>
      dominated the sport for a while in the 18th century. The cricket ground at
      <a href="/wiki/Arundel_Castle_Cricket_Ground" title="Arundel Castle Cricket Ground">
       Arundel Castle
      </a>
      traditionally plays host to a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duchess_of_Norfolk" title="Duchess of Norfolk">
       Duchess of Norfolk
      </a>
      's XI which plays the national
      <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">
       test
      </a>
      sides touring England.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        [108]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        [109]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The sport of stoolball is also associated with Sussex, which has a claim to be where the sport originated and certainly where its revival took place in the early 20th century. Sussex is represented in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League" title="Football League">
       Football League
      </a>
      by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion" title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion">
       Brighton &amp; Hove Albion
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Crawley_Town_F.C." title="Crawley Town F.C.">
       Crawley Town
      </a>
      . Brighton has been a League member since 1920, whereas Crawley was promoted to the League in 2011. Sussex has had its own
      <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County_Football_Association" title="Sussex County Football Association">
       football association
      </a>
      , since 1882
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1st100_113-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-1st100-113">
        [110]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and its own
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sussex_County_League" title="Sussex County League">
       football league
      </a>
      , which has since expanded into Surrey, since 1920.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCFLAbout_114-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SCFLAbout-114">
        [111]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In horse racing, Sussex is home to
      <a href="/wiki/Goodwood_Racecourse" title="Goodwood Racecourse">
       Goodwood
      </a>
      , Fontwell Park,
      <a href="/wiki/Brighton_Racecourse" title="Brighton Racecourse">
       Brighton
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Plumpton_Racecourse" title="Plumpton Racecourse">
       Plumpton
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/All_England_Jumping_Course_at_Hickstead" title="All England Jumping Course at Hickstead">
       All England Jumping Course
      </a>
      show jumping facility at Hickstead is situated 8 miles (13 km) north of Brighton and Hove.
     </p>
     <p>
      In Arlington, near Eastbourne, the local stadium is home to the Eastbourne Eagles speedway team, who race in the UK's top flight of speedway, the Elite League. Stock Car racing is also held at the same venue.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
       Cuisine
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sussex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sussex_Pond_Pudding_2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Sussex_Pond_Pudding_2.jpg/220px-Sussex_Pond_Pudding_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Sussex_Pond_Pudding_2.jpg/330px-Sussex_Pond_Pudding_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Sussex_Pond_Pudding_2.jpg/440px-Sussex_Pond_Pudding_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sussex_Pond_Pudding_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Sliced Sussex Pond Pudding
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The historic county is known for its "seven good things of Sussex".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
       <a href="#cite_note-115">
        [112]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        [113]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        [114]
       </a>
      </sup>
      These seven things are Pulborough eel, Selsey cockle, Chichester lobster, Rye herring, Arundel mullet, Amberley trout and Bourne
      <a href="/wiki/Wheatear" title="Wheatear">
       wheatear
      </a>
      . Sussex is also known for Ashdown Partridge Pudding,
      <a href="/wiki/Chiddingly" title="Chiddingly">
       Chiddingly
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Hot_pot" title="Hot pot">
       Hot pot
      </a>
      , Sussex Bacon Pudding, Sussex Hogs' Pudding, Huffed Chicken, Sussex Churdles, Sussex Shepherds Pie,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sussex_Pond_Pudding" title="Sussex Pond Pudding">
       Sussex Pond Pudding
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        [115]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sussex Blanket Pudding, Sussex Well Pudding, and Chichester Pudding. Sussex is also known for its cakes and biscuits known as Sussex Plum Heavies
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        [116]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Sussex Lardy Johns, while
      <a href="/wiki/Banoffee_pie" title="Banoffee pie">
       banoffee pie
      </a>
      was first created in 1972 in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jevington" title="Jevington">
       Jevington
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ArgBP_120-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ArgBP-120">
        [117]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NGDishes_121-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NGDishes-121">
        [118]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The county has vineyards and the 18th century beer brewers,
      <a href="/wiki/Harveys_Brewery" title="Harveys Brewery">
       Harveys of Lewes
      </a>
      as well as many more recently established breweries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        [119]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In recent decades Sussex wines have gained international acclaim winning awards including the 2006 Best Sparkling Wine in the World at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decanter_World_Wine_Awards" title="Decanter World Wine Awards">
       Decanter World Wine Awards
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VisitSx-Wine_123-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-VisitSx-Wine-123">
        [120]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many vineyards make wines using traditional
      <a href="/wiki/Champagne" title="Champagne">
       Champagne
      </a>
      varieties and methods,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndWin_124-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-IndWin-124">
        [121]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and there are similarities between the topography and chalk and clay soils
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxLifeWin_125-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxLifeWin-125">
        [122]
       </a>
      </sup>
      of Sussex downland and that of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Champagne_region" title="Champagne region">
       Champagne region
      </a>
      which lies on a latitude 100 miles (161 km) to the south.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndWin_124-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-IndWin-124">
        [121]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCC_126-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TCC-126">
        [123]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">
       Visual arts
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sussex&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Visual arts">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Long_Man_of_Wilmington.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2272" data-file-width="1704" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Long_Man_of_Wilmington.jpg/170px-Long_Man_of_Wilmington.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Long_Man_of_Wilmington.jpg/255px-Long_Man_of_Wilmington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Long_Man_of_Wilmington.jpg/340px-Long_Man_of_Wilmington.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Long_Man_of_Wilmington.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Long Man of Wilmington is Europe's largest representation of the human form
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Some of the earliest known art in Sussex is the carvings in the galleries of the
      <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">
       Neolithic
      </a>
      flint mines at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cissbury" title="Cissbury">
       Cissbury
      </a>
      on the South Downs near Worthing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UBth-FM_127-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UBth-FM-127">
        [124]
       </a>
      </sup>
      From the Roman period, the palace at
      <a href="/wiki/Fishbourne_Roman_Palace" title="Fishbourne Roman Palace">
       Fishbourne
      </a>
      has the largest in situ collection of
      <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">
       mosaics
      </a>
      in the UK,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxPast.3DFb_128-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxPast.3DFb-128">
        [125]
       </a>
      </sup>
      while the villa at
      <a href="/wiki/Bignor_Roman_Villa" title="Bignor Roman Villa">
       Bignor
      </a>
      contains some of the best preserved
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_mosaic" title="Roman mosaic">
       Roman mosaics
      </a>
      in England.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HTBignor_129-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HTBignor-129">
        [126]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Dating from around the 12th century, the 'Lewes Group' of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wall_painting" title="Wall painting">
       wall paintings
      </a>
      can be found in several churches across the centre of Sussex, some of which are celebrated for their age, extent and quality. Of uncertain origin, the
      <a href="/wiki/Long_Man_of_Wilmington" title="Long Man of Wilmington">
       Long Man of Wilmington
      </a>
      is Europe’s largest representation of the human form.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxPast-LM_130-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxPast-LM-130">
        [127]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the late 18th century three men commissioned important works of the county which ensured that its landscapes and daily life were captured onto canvas.
      <a href="/wiki/Sir_William_Burrell,_2nd_Baronet" title="Sir William Burrell, 2nd Baronet">
       William Burrell
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Knepp_Castle" title="Knepp Castle">
       Knepp Castle
      </a>
      commissioned Swiss-born watercolourist
      <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Hieronymus_Grimm" title="Samuel Hieronymus Grimm">
       Samuel Hieronymus Grimm
      </a>
      to tour Sussex, producing 900 watercolours of the county's buildings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SRS_131-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SRS-131">
        [128]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/George_Wyndham,_3rd_Earl_of_Egremont" title="George Wyndham, 3rd Earl of Egremont">
       George Wyndham, 3rd Earl of Egremont
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Petworth_House" title="Petworth House">
       Petworth House
      </a>
      was a patron of painters such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JMW_Turner" title="JMW Turner">
       JMW Turner
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/John_Constable" title="John Constable">
       John Constable
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SDNP-PP_132-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SDNP-PP-132">
        [129]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_%27Mad_Jack%27_Fuller" title="John 'Mad Jack' Fuller">
       John 'Mad Jack' Fuller
      </a>
      also commissioned Turner to make a series of paintings which resulted in thirteen finished watercolours of Fuller's house at
      <a href="/wiki/Brightling" title="Brightling">
       Brightling
      </a>
      and the area around it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BM-Turner_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BM-Turner-133">
        [130]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chichester_Canal_(1828).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="332" data-file-width="730" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Chichester_Canal_%281828%29.jpg/250px-Chichester_Canal_%281828%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Chichester_Canal_%281828%29.jpg/375px-Chichester_Canal_%281828%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Chichester_Canal_%281828%29.jpg/500px-Chichester_Canal_%281828%29.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chichester_Canal_(1828).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Chichester Canal by JMW Turner
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the 19th century landscape watercolourist
      <a href="/wiki/Copley_Fielding" title="Copley Fielding">
       Copley Fielding
      </a>
      lived in Sussex and illustrator
      <a href="/wiki/Aubrey_Beardsley" title="Aubrey Beardsley">
       Aubrey Beardsley
      </a>
      and painter and sculptor
      <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gill" title="Eric Gill">
       Eric Gill
      </a>
      were born in Brighton. Gill went on to found an
      <a href="/wiki/Art_colony" title="Art colony">
       art colony
      </a>
      in Ditchling known as
      <a href="/wiki/The_Guild_of_St_Joseph_and_St_Dominic" title="The Guild of St Joseph and St Dominic">
       The Guild of St Joseph and St Dominic
      </a>
      , which survived until 1989. The 1920s and 1930s saw the creation of some of the best-known works by
      <a href="/wiki/Edward_Burra" title="Edward Burra">
       Edward Burra
      </a>
      who was known for his work of Sussex, Paris and Harlem
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guard-Burra_134-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Guard-Burra-134">
        [131]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Eric_Ravilious" title="Eric Ravilious">
       Eric Ravilious
      </a>
      who is known for his paintings of the South Downs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SxLife-Rav_135-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SxLife-Rav-135">
        [132]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the early 20th century
      <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Bell" title="Vanessa Bell">
       Vanessa Bell
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Grant" title="Duncan Grant">
       Duncan Grant
      </a>
      , both members of the
      <a href="/wiki/Bloomsbury_Group" title="Bloomsbury Group">
       Bloomsbury Group
      </a>
      , lived and worked at
      <a href="/wiki/Charleston_Farmhouse" title="Charleston Farmhouse">
       Charleston Farmhouse
      </a>
      near
      <a href="/wiki/Firle" title="Firle">
       Firle
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charleston_136-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Charleston-136">
        [133]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sussex also became a major centre for
      <a href="/wiki/Surrealism" title="Surrealism">
       surrealism
      </a>
      in the early 20th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pall-Surr_137-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Pall-Surr-137">
        [134]
       </a>
      </sup>
      At
      <a href="/wiki/West_Dean,_West_Sussex" title="West Dean, West Sussex">
       West Dean
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edward_James" title="Edward James">
       Edward James
      </a>
      was patron to artists including
      <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Dal%C3%AD" title="Salvador Dalí">
       Salvador Dalí
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Magritte" title="René Magritte">
       René Magritte
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pall-Surr_137-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Pall-Surr-137">
        [134]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDnColl_138-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WDnColl-138">
        [135]
       </a>
      </sup>
      while at
      <a href="/wiki/Farley_Farm_House" title="Farley Farm House">
       Farley Farm House
      </a>
      near
      <a href="/wiki/Chiddingly" title="Chiddingly">
       Chiddingly
      </a>
      the home of
      <a href="/wiki/Roland_Penrose" title="Roland Penrose">
       Roland Penrose
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lee_Miller" title="Lee Miller">
       Lee Miller
      </a>
      was frequented by artists such as
      <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">
       Pablo Picasso
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Man_Ray" title="Man Ray">
       Man Ray
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">
       Henry Moore
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eileen_Agar" title="Eileen Agar">
       Eileen Agar
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jean_Dubuffet" title="Jean Dubuffet">
       Jean Dubuffet
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Dorothea_Tanning" title="Dorothea Tanning">
       Dorothea Tanning
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Max_Ernst" title="Max Ernst">
       Max Ernst
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pall-Surr_137-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Pall-Surr-137">
        [134]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FFHse_139-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FFHse-139">
        [136]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Both collections form one of the most important bodies of Surrealist art in Europe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pall.3DSurrSx_140-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Pall.3DSurrSx-140">
        [137]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">
       Footnotes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
